If I could give this salon 10 stars, I would! Therapy offers a wide variety of services, using high quality products, at very reasonable prices. The owner, Sarah, does my hair and she specializes in high quality hair color and cutting techniques. She is honest, is impeccable with a scissor and color, and can help you figure out the right style for your face shape! The salon carries all Aveda products and this also includes makeup and body lotions as well as facial cleaners and candles. I can spend all day in this salon it feels like a day spa. I am beyond in love with this salon and I am always recommending it to my friends and colleagues. I promise you that you will not regret giving it a try. I can assure you that once you try it you will have found your new forever salon. Sarah, the salon owner, is sweet, honest, caring, and fun to talk to during my hair appointments, and most importantly she is very giving. < Text>
The food at Hong Kong Chinese Restaurant has always been very fresh and hot.  The visual appeal tells me how fresh everything is.  The taste of freshness and wonderful flavors backs up the visual appeal.  The Hot and Sour Soup is rich and full of fresh Shiitake mushrooms.  The Pot Stickers are to die for in my book - full of savory meat, not doughy at all, but golden brown with a crispness along with the juiciness of each bite.  The Won Ton Soup is so simply wonderful, that I must have it when I occasionally don't feel great - that chicken broth heals.  The Kung Pao Chicken  is crunchy, wonderfully flavorful, and of course, fresh!   Can't wait to try other dishes....</Text>

<Name>Teresa Bui<//Name><Time>1576994089210</Time><Rate>5< /Rate><Review>I love hot yoga, - it helps strengthen the body,  cleanse the pores but also provides a place of self reflection and focus in a world full of distraction.

The teachers at Zuda have been great, they push you to your best, but they also don't judge you when you are struggling. The studio itself
is gorgeous : simple yet modern, airy and white with a nice wood flooring.  There's 2 bathrooms, water refill station, dressing rooms and showers. There's 2 hour free parking nearby.

You sign up for classes online and reserve your mat space and they put a block and mat for you already. Some classes are more packed than others, the one with Anne Marie (the studio owner) teaching is always packed so come a few minutes early. I love it when they have live music inside the studio.

The only thing is that they don't always explain how to do a pose. There's lots that you can look to your neighbors for guidance but some others poses such as crow or handstand, you either have to learn on your own, or ask after class.

They have $30 for 30 days for new students, so check it out!<//Review><pics>None<//pics>< resp>

<Rate>5< /Rate>< text>
Zuda was my first time ever doing hot yoga! Their intro deal is $30 for 30 days. It's a great way to try the different instructors and different class levels and styles. I'm not personally too familiar with the practice of yoga, but had done it before and was familiar with the different poses. When in doubt I just take a look around at others! I'm a big fan of Lindsey and Kenny. I have noticed a difference in the class levels, in that level 1 classes the instructors will explain a bit more. Overall I think even beginners would be fine and able to go at their own pace and take what they need in more advanced classes. Some of the weekday evening classes can get really packed and they have a new system where you reserve a specific spot in the room on the app. The front staff is great and very welcoming. The studio is very clean and well kept. I highly recommend trying Zuda out! Definitely hydrate all day and during and take breaks when you need.< /text>

< Review>
I started going to Zuda at the invitation of a close friend. I've only attended weekend morning classes so far but definitely thinking of signing up for a membership and branching out to more days. I'm excited to bring my daughter for a Sunday kids class, when we can both get our workout in, at the same time and under the same roof. I have enjoyed the full-class feeling and energy of the studio. It is well lit and smells clean, despite all of sweat that pours off of me each class. I enjoy the variety of music, some modern but appropriately chosen for the mood, and some more spiritual or tribal sounding - both types lend well to the energy of each set of exercises during the class. The teachers I've sampled have been consistent in teaching flavor and feel like good guides as I drop in to my body in each session. The all-levels class has a good mix of challenging add-on moves that can take any pose to the next level. Teachers encourage students to only do what they feel is right for their body that day, so I have not felt pressured to exceed my capabilities just to keep up with the class. Well done Zuda!</Review>

<Pictures>None</Pictures><UserId.>116319882164823258457</UserId.>< text>
I really like Zuda yoga for many reasons- they heat up the room during practice to just the right temp, hot enough to get a great sweat, but not so much you're feeling suffocated. The main studio has awesome floors, sweet audio system, and they keep it clean. The teachers have an upbeat and positive vibe and the flow sequences are well-thought out usually. Plus you always leave feeling like you got a great workout (plus I sleep better!) The assistants give exquisite adjustments!

I recently moved from Washington DC, and the one thing I miss about my old studio is the dab of essential oil the teacher would give each student before class; it wasn't about the oil but about the teacher making a quick connection to each student. I also miss the teacher cuing to turn and say hello to each neighbor to "break the ice" before class. This lack of connection between teachers/ students leaves me often feeling like the teachers at Zuda will never know who I am or my name, and it's hard to connect with other students around you. I realize I may need to assert myself more, but it doesn't seem the studio really cultivates those opportunities very well-- and I can compare that to my regular studio in DC that did a great job of that. Those would be my recommendations! Keep up the AMAZING work!< /text>

<Rate>5</Rate>< review>
I have LOVED my experience at Zuda Yoga.  I have tried several other studios in the area, and this one is far and away the best I have been to.  They have an awesome introductory deal ($30 for unlimited yoga in your first month) that some other studios offer as well, but this is the first studio I will continue with once my first month expires.  The instructors are positive, friendly, and extremely welcoming and seem to all have great playlists.  The studio offers lots of classes throughout the day and has a clean, bright, and friendly vibe.  The class sizes are quite large, which is sometimes an issue at other studios but at Zuda seems to just add to the group dynamic.  Make sure to bring your own yoga mat and towel (they are each $5 to rent, which is significantly more expensive than other places I‚Äôve been), but they‚Äôll allow you to borrow for free on your first class.  Also, there is only 1 shower, but people are quick and I never end up waiting long.  Overall it‚Äôs a great studio and I would recommend to anyone I know!</review>

< Text>
I did the 30 days for $30 membership to introduce myself to the studio and to get back into yoga. I previously had experience doing vinyasa yoga so even though I did the ‚ÄúAll Levels‚Äù classes, I quickly learned that most of the instructors do not teach at a basic level and you need to know the names of the poses- if you don‚Äôt, you can always take a look around and there‚Äôs no shame in that! I have consistently been going to the 6am classes for over 3 weeks now, learning the different styles of three different instructors that teach in the mornings. I love that each instructor has a very different style of flows- Jen is fast-paced, challenging, a tough workout; Ann Marie (the owner) does poses that I have never heard of before, gives time for meditation, and does a routine ‚Äúdo it yourself‚Äù core workout; Jess is a bit in between, but I like her style the most because she has an ease to her that makes you feel more comfortable about going in child‚Äôs pose if you need to. I also really love that they always have an assistant going around, I just wish she could help me more- there‚Äôs usually too many people to go around! Overall, I‚Äôm really pleased with my experience at Zuda so far. I love sweating (a lot!) each morning and I am definitely getting stronger, physically and mentally. Unfortunately, I don‚Äôt think I‚Äôll be able to afford their monthly membership. If only it were a little cheaper! Thank you Zuda!< /Text>

<text>Zuda is yoga, workout, church, and chapel. Seriously, this is a community yoga centre, with so much more than just yoga. Everyone here breathes energy and spirit, truly embodying peace, power, hard work, dedication, and love. I've never felt this energy at another yoga studio, and it keeps me coming back for more.

The classes vary in style and difficulty. They tend to get packed -- and if you're open-minded, you start to like that. Everyone moving together in moving mediation, energy flowing around the room. They keep the rooms heated, but in winter especially, this is super comfortable. I find that it's to a great level that allows me to get deeper into my poses and to feel rejuvenated afterwards, without totally draining me of all my water the way hot yoga tends to. The instructors are the best of the best. My favorites are Joel and Jess, but they're all amazing! The assistants really help you explore those extra inches in your poses and give the BEST massages while you're in them.

The system here is geared towards helping each person explore whatever it is they need to explore. There's also assistant training, teacher training, flight school, sisterhood circle, and even a yoga retreat to Bali. Seriously, it doesn't get better.

Introductory rate is 30 days for $30. You can't beat that. And, if you come consistently enough, you will start to feel the incredible power of Zuda within you. Come by, give it a whirl, be open minded, and let it change your life!<//text><Time>1520315043148< /Time></record></dataset><record>

<time>1556149006526</time><Rate>4< /Rate><Text>I like this yoga studio, it's clean and convenient for me but I do have some important things to say. This studio does NOT seem like it's meant for beginners, if you've had zero yoga classes, I don't think you should start here! I've done just a few bikram hot yoga classes before and I discovered, of course, that Vinyasa is harder because it is a faster pace. Not all of the classes, level 1 or all levels,  go over yoga poses! So if you are new I suggest you sit in the back to be able to watch others.

I do love that the Zuda yoga studios are non judgemental and you can really do whatever you want. It's just if you are waiting for someone to help or correct your pose, it most likely won't happen. I haven't had any pose help from the assistants, but I do get massages! If you're comfortable with just going with the flow and flip flopping around as beginner then you'll be okay at this studio! lol This place is convenient for me and it has gotten me used to practicing around a lot of people. I like how you can reserve your yoga mat spot before the classes, ever since they started the new booking method, there has been less people in classes! < review>
Good, but nothing spectacular. Will i return? Sure. They add to the bill an automatic 20% gratuity + another percentage for the workers' benefit (i forgot what they call it). <name>Gabriel Hayes</name>< date>
1617337864258< /date>
<Rate>4< /Rate>< text>
Great atmosphere and service, food was a bit "meh"...

I'm going to chock this up to the fact that we came at the end of the night on a Thursday. Not that this makes it ok, but we'll give it another shot.

The hummus as an app was "ok" but could use way more spices - the toppings were nice and fresh though. We would have liked it to come with some fresh veg as well (carrots/etc to dip) as the ratio of hummus to pita that they give is way off.

My wife ordered the prime rib, which was a good generous portion, but again, it didn't seem to have much seasoning  (nor did the marbled potatoes).

I ordered a pizza (ham, pineapple and jalapeno that is on the menu) and it too seemed bland (are you seeing a pattern yet?). The toppings on the pizza were generous, however the crust was not very crispy.

Service was pretty quick and our server was very nice and thoughtful.

Something to note - tip is included in the bill, and they don't ask you to sign your credit card receipt. I don't like either of these things. I tip WELL for good service, and I tip for mediocre service. If a restaurant FORCES a tip on the customer, then just remove the tip and raise your price, and pay your staff more per hour. That left a sour taste in my mouth. And the fact that I didn't have to sign for a bill of more than $100 offers very little protection for either party - just poor practice in my opinion.

Like I said, we'll give it another shot, but I'm not getting my hopes up.</text>

It's 2021. Stay at home order extended indefinitely. Political unrest in the nation's capitol. This coincides with my Mom's birthday. She says  as she is flumoxed by the world situation. " Oh, just order a pizza_"..

If they had a feedback page, I would share these comments there, however, there is no feedback page, so here goes.

The Good
-Very tasty food.
-Excellent spicing.
-Fast

The Not So Good
- The carnitas were excellent except for the taste of griddle shortening peaking through.
- The Chile Relleno and beans were also very tasty except for the Chile pepper itself, which I could not cut without getting a sharp knife and took a long time to chew.  My guess is that it was frozen and quickly defrosted and sauced.  This problem could have been because of the pandemic ‚Äî no way to tell how many orders of what to expect.  Should be a more effective way to defrost a pepper.

This place could be amazing.</text>

<username>Michael Shaffer< /username><user_id>100261157084506635178< /user_id>< review>
Our process started in the fall of 2019.  Chuck came by and presented me with Solar Negotiators' proposal.
Chuck's presentation was easily understood, he was able to satisfactorily answer all my questions.  I had decided in favor of Solar Negotiators over the two other competitors I had met with.
Unfortunately I just wasn't quite ready to pull the trigger.  Fast forward to now, the fall of 2020.
My wife had scheduled three contractors to interview.  Chuck was first.  Near the end of his presentation I took my wife aside and asked her, "Do you think we need to see the other two contractors?"  She said, "Nope".
We signed Chuck and Solar Negotiators up and canceled the other two.
In very short order materials were scheduled to arrive, emails for permissions were received, the lead installer came by for a site visit and then the schedule was moved forward, next thing I new it was done.
Very professional, very clean and easy to talk to.
Shareen has just come by to present us with a fully functional system and demonstrate all the internet based and cell phone app based options to monitor all aspects of our system.
In short, Solar Negotiators have got their game down.  Honest, fair and without that "Used car salesmen" type of sales pressure.
I encourage invite you to join my wife and I to become a member of the Solar Negotiators' family!< /review>

So I was somewhat disappointed with the service I received today. <name>R Moore<//name><Time>1556222937125</Time><Rate>3</Rate><Review>I finally decided to get solar and knew I wanted a local company to do the installation.  I spent months researching and finally decided to go with Solar Negotiators (Now Solar Maintenance Pros), as they were local, had great reviews, and the owner was a Veteran, being a Veteran myself this played a big role.  I'll leave names out just to keep things as objective as possible.

I met with my sales representative and planned out my system.  I was paying cash as I didn't want to hassle with yet another loan.  As everyone who goes solar knows, it's a big investment and something that isn't taken lightly.  From this point, I was thoroughly satisfied with the process.

My project got turned over to the service team and I was assigned a service representative to oversee my project and be my point of contact from here on out.  This was February 22, 2019.  From here I was given the checklist and approximate timelines.

The Site Survey went off without any problems.  The plans were submitted and I signed off on it.  A few days later I was told there were problems with my plans and they sent over a second draft for my approval.  I signed the second draft and awaited install day.

Install day came and when I got home I noticed the panels were in the wrong area.  Long story short, the original plans were given to the installers, not the newest approved plans.  After a little back and forth, I think they did a great job on resolving this issue.  Instead of moving the rack, they just added a new rack and gave me 2 free panels to offset the shade issue and as a way to make up for the confusion on their end.

My system went from 4.7kW to 5.2kW.  Therefore it had to go back to the city for approval, which delayed the process.  I'm 62 days into my project; I have panels on my roof, an inverter on my wall, a brand new electrical panel and I'm still getting all my electricity from PG&E.  I'm just waiting to find out what the next step is, I've reached out and haven't got any communication back.

So all this to say the following:  I wish Solar Maintenance Pros did a better job with communication.  Maybe not everyday, but send an email at least every other day with a status, even if it's just "still waiting on the city to approve your project".  I worked in the service industry and I called my customer's everyday to let them know what was going on with their computer, they appreciated the constant communication.  It reassured them and let them know that their computer/project was important.  People want to know what's going on, especially with a project that costs so much.  This is a huge investment, I am by no means wealthy, so this took me a long time to save up for.  I don't like being left out in the dark.<//Review><pictures>None</pictures><resp>None</resp><gmap_id>0x8094661ba5ae344b:0x401869785e64d343< /gmap_id></record></dataset><record>

<UserId.>104391982512389412908<//UserId.><user_name>Scott Herrell<//user_name><Time>1557966117990<//Time>< rating>
5<//rating>
< text>
This was a long researched project for us. We spent over 2 years researching & interviewing multiple solar installers. The price ranges from Sunrun, Tesla, etc were huge. Some were twice the price of Solar Negotiators!!

Our project was unique but not impossible and we needed some special things done for optimal production of our ground mount solar panels.

Again and again when we found the panels we wanted, the installation was too expensive. Then when we found an affordable installer he wanted use cheap solar panels or had bad reviews or wasn't local.

So here is how we made our decision.
Ask these questions:

How are their reviews on google, yelp, etc?
Are they a local company?
Are they knowledgeable on solar?
Do they come out and inspect the install site or use google earth?
How many installations have they done?
How often do they clean the panels?
What kind of warranty do they provide for loss production on the panels?

Happy to say Solar Negotiators checked all the boxes. We could not be happier with our experience with the install and customer service. They love what they do and it shows in their work and attention to detail.

I would highly recommend them to any of my closest friends.

**Remember that 2019 is the last year of the full 30% Fed Rebate**.

Scott H
O'Neals, Ca</text>
